- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the letter-is-spirit line exists because the most persuasive violations arrive dressed as spirit, tests-after achieve the same goals, it's about spirit not ritual, so the skill closes the loophole by defining the ritual as the spirit

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed one generic engineer stands where the skill's own bug-fix example traces the natural journey, an empty email accepted in production, the fixer writes the rejecting test first, watches it fail with expected Email required got undefined, implements the two-line guard, watches it pass, and considers extraction only after green, the whole cycle in four artifacts and two gate runs
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the journey works because the bug itself becomes the test specification, a reproduced failure is a requirement statement with proof built in, which is why the skill's debugging integration says never fix bugs without a test
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the journey's failure branch is the direct patch, guard added first, test after or never, leaving no proof the guard addresses the reported case and no tripwire when a refactor later drops it
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: journeys through this skill's cycle, session interruption journeys belong to the retainer themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to recast the scenario as the bug-to-test round trip using the skill's own empty-email example as the trace
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the bug-fix case is TDD's cleanest sell because the failing test costs nothing extra, the bug must be reproduced to be fixed anyway, and encoding the reproduction as a test converts a one-time diagnostic into a permanent regression guard, the skill's never-fix-without-a-test rule is thus its easiest law to justify economically

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed symbol-count boundary misprices this node's work, whose units are the sunk 371-line read in under an hour, per-loop cycle overhead, a witnessed red, a minimal green, both gates, minutes each at the skill's intended grain, per-violation deletion cost, hours occasionally, the enforcement's real price, and per-audit checks led by the cheap equality test
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the skill's economics concentrate cost at violations rather than at compliance, clean loops are cheap and deletions are expensive, an incentive design where the costly path is the one the law forbids
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: pricing TDD by its violation cost, the feared deletion, rather than its compliance cost, minutes per loop, is exactly the sunk-cost framing the skill's arguments dismantle, the deletion is the price of having violated, not of practicing
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: budgeting this node's upkeep and the cycle's operation, corpus assignment budgets stay in the seed rows
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to restate the model in its four units, sunk read, per-loop minutes, violation-priced deletions, and equality-led audits
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the skill's minimal-code doctrine is itself a workload rule, the green phase's just-enough discipline caps each loop's implementation cost by construction, YAGNI enforced at the loop level keeps loops small, keeps failures local, and makes the deletion penalty survivable when it fires, the law's harshness is funded by the cycle's smallness
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to budget loops at minutes, keep them small enough that deletion never exceeds a loop's cost, and let violations price themselves
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the skill's economics concentrate cost at violations rather than at compliance, clean loops are cheap and deletions are expensive, an incentive design where the costly path is the one the law forbids

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed corpus-process bullets stand beside what the skill rules for cycle failures, a wrong-failure red loops back to red until the test fails for the right reason, a failing green fixes code, never the test, other tests breaking at green are fixed now, not deferred, a violation discovered mid-stream triggers deletion and restart rather than salvage, and repeated stuck states route through the when-stuck table toward design simplification, not toward gate relaxation
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because every response channels pressure away from the law and into the work, the gates absorb retries, the design absorbs complexity, and the law itself is never the adjustable part, backpressure by architecture
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the erosion path is retrying against the gate instead of the work, loosening what counts as a proper failure or a pristine pass after repeated frustration, the gate quietly recalibrated by fatigue
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: failure-response doctrine for the cycle, journal-repair doctrine belongs to the retainer themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the response rules, red loops to red, green fixes code, breakage fixes now, violations delete, stuckness simplifies design
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the when-stuck table's diagnosis is the skill's most constructive move, every stuck state is read as a design signal, hard to test means hard to use, must mock everything means too coupled, huge setup means simplify, converting the practitioner's frustration into architecture feedback, the cycle as a design linter that happens to produce tests

- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the cycle's tests assert behavior, and performance assertions in unit cycles produce flaky gates, timing variance breaking red-green determinism, so the skill's silence is a scoping decision consistent with its one-behavior test doctrine
